the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n    51→ *\n    52→ * <p>\n    53→ * It is a requirement that the processing logic ({@link Topology}) be defined in a deterministic way,\n    54→ * as in, the order in which all operators are added must be predictable and the same across all application\n    55→ * instances.\n    56→ * Topologies are only identical if all operators are added in the same order.\n    57→ * If different {@link KafkaStreams} instances of the same application build different topologies the result may be\n    58→ * incompatible runtime code and unexpected results or errors\n    59→ *\n    60→ * @see Topology\n    61→ * @see KStream\n    62→ * @see KTable\n    63→ * @see GlobalKTable\n    64→ */\n    65→public class StreamsBuilder {\n    66→\n    67→    /** The actual topology that is constructed by this StreamsBuilder. */\n    68→    protected final Topology topology;\n    69→\n    70→    /** The topology's internal builder. */\n    71→    protected final InternalTopologyBuilder internalTopologyBuilder;\n    72→\n    73→    protected final InternalStreamsBuilder internalStreamsBuilder;\n    74→\n    75→    public StreamsBuilder() {\n    76→        topology = new Topology();\n    77→        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n    78→        internalStreamsBuilder = new InternalStreamsBuilder(internalTopologyBuilder, false);\n    79→    }\n    80→\n    81→    /**\n    82→     * Create a {@code StreamsBuilder} instance.\n    83→     *\n    84→     * @param cannot be {@code null}\n   132→     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n   133→     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topic\n   134→     */\n   135→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final String topic,\n   136→                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   137→        return stream(Collections.singleton(topic), consumed);\n   138→    }\n   139→\n   140→    /**\n   141→     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topics.\n   142→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, default {@link TimestampExtractor}, and default key and value\n   143→     * deserializers as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   144→     * <p>\n   145→     * If multiple topics are specified there is no ordering guarantee for records from different topics.\n   146→     * <p>\n   147→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   148→     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n   149→     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n   150→     *\n   151→     * @param topics the topic names; This also means that the work\n   188→     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n   189→     * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n   190→     * <p>\n   191→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   192→     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n   193→     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n   194→     *\n   195→     * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n   196→     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n   197→     */\n   198→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n   199→        return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n   200→    }\n   201→\n   202→    /**\n   203→     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n   204→     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n   205→     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n   206→     * <p>\n   207→     * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n   208→     * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. This also means that the work\n   209→     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n   210→     * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n   211→     * <p>\n   212→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   213→     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n   214→     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n   215→     *\n   216→     * @param topicPattern  the pattern to match for topic names\n   217→     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n   218→     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n   219→     */\n   220→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern,\n   221→                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   222→        Objects.requireNonNull(topicPattern, \"topicPattern can't be null\");\n   223→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   224→        return internalStreamsBuilder.stream(topicPattern, new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed));\n   225→    }\n   226→\n   227→    /**\n   228→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   229→     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n   230→     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n   231→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   232→     * <p>\n   233→     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n   234→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   235→     * <p>\n   236→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} using the given\n   237→     * {@code Materialized} instance.\n   238→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   239→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   240→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   241→     * <p>\n   242→     * You should only specify serdes in the {@link Consumed} instance as these will also be used to overwrite the\n   243→     * serdes in {@link Materialized}, i.e.,\n   244→     * <pre> {@code\n   245→     * streamBuilder.table(topic, Consumed.with(Serde.String(), Serde.String()), Materialized.<String, String, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>as(storeName))\n   246→     * }\n   247→     * </pre>\n   248→     * To query the local {@link ReadOnlyKeyValueStore} it must be obtained via\n   249→     * {@link KafkaStreams#store(StoreQueryParameters) KafkaStreams#store(...)}:\n   250→     * <pre>{@code\n   251→     * KafkaStreams streams = ...\n   252→     * StoreQueryParameters<ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>>> storeQueryParams = StoreQueryParameters.fromNameAndType(queryableStoreName, QueryableStoreTypes.timestampedKeyValueStore());\n   253→     * ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>> localStore = streams.store(storeQueryParams);\n   254→     * K key = \"some-key\";\n   255→     * ValueAndTimestamp<V> valueForKey = localStore.get(key); // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n   256→     * }</pre>\n   257→     * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n   258→     * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n   259→     *\n   260→     * @param topic              the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   261→     * @param consumed           the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters; cannot be {@code null}\n   262→     * @param materialized       the instance of {@link Materialized} used to materialize a state store; cannot be {@code null}\n   263→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   264→     */\n   265→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   266→                                                  final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\n   267→                                                  final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n   268→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   269→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   270→        Objects.requireNonNull(materialized, \"materialized can't be null\");\n   271→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal = new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed);\n   272→        materialized.withKeySerde(consumedInternal.keySerde()).withValueSerde(consumedInternal.valueSerde());\n   273→\n   274→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   275→            new MaterializedInternal<>(materialized, internalStreamsBuilder, topic + \"-\");\n   276→\n   277→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   278→    }\n   279→\n   280→    /**\n   281→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   282→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy and default key and value deserializers as specified in the\n   283→     * {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   284→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   285→     * <p>\n   286→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   287→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   288→     * <p>\n   289→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n   290→     * store name. Note that store name may not be queryable through Interactive Queries.\n   291→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   292→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   293→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   294→     *\n   295→     * @param topic the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   296→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   297→     */\n   298→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic) {\n   299→        return table(topic, Consumed.with(null, null));\n   300→    }\n   301→\n   302→    /**\n   303→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   304→     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n   305→     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n   306→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   307→     * <p>\n   308→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   309→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   310→     * <p>\n   311→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n   312→     * store name. Note that store name may not be queryable through Interactive Queries.\n   313→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   314→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   315→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   316→     *\n   317→     * @param topic     the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   318→     * @param consumed  the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters; cannot be {@code null}\n   319→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   320→     */\n   321→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   322→                                                  final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   323→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   324→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   325→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal = new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed);\n   326→\n   327→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   328→            new MaterializedInternal<>(\n   329→                Materialized.with(consumedInternal.keySerde(), consumedInternal.valueSerde()),\n   330→                internalStreamsBuilder,\n   331→                topic + \"-\");\n   332→\n   333→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   334→    }\n   335→\n   336→    /**\n   337→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   338→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   339→     * Key and value deserializers as defined by the options in {@link Materialized} are used.\n   340→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   341→     * <p>\n   342→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   343→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   344→     * <p>\n   345→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} using the {@link Materialized} instance.\n   346→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   347→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   348→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   349→     *\n   350→     * @param topic         the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   351→     * @param materialized  the instance of {@link Materialized} used to materialize a state store; cannot be {@code null}\n   352→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   353→     */\n   354→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   355→                                                  final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n   356→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   357→        Objects.requireNonNull(materialized, \"materialized can't be null\");\n   358→\n   359→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   360→            new MaterializedInternal<>(materialized, internalStreamsBuilder, topic + \"-\");\n   361→\n   362→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal =\n   363→                new ConsumedInternal<>(Consumed.with(materializedInternal.keySerde(), materializedInternal.valueSerde()));\n   364→\n   365→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   366→    }\n   367→\n   368→    /**\n   369→     * Create a {@link GlobalKTable} for the specified topic.\n   370→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   371→     * <p>\n   372→     * The resulting {@link GlobalKTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n   373→     * store name. Note that store name may not be queryable through Interactive Queries.\n   374→     * No internal changelog topic is created since the original input topic can be used for recovery (cf.\n   375→     * methods of {@link KGroupedStream} and {@link KGroupedTable} that return a {@link KTable}).\n   376→     * <p>\n   377→     * Note that {@link GlobalKTable} always applies {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy {@code \"earliest\"}\n   378→     * regardless of the specified value in {@link StreamsConfig} or {@link Consumed}.\n   379→     * Furthermore, {@link GlobalKTable} cannot be a {@link org.apache.kafka.streams.state.VersionedBytesStoreSupplier\n   380→     * versioned state store}.\n   381→     *\n   382→     * @param topic the topic name;                     final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\n   461→                                                              final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n   462→ Creating a single {@link Processor} object\n   545→     * and returning the same object reference in {@link ProcessorSupplier#get()} is a\n   546→     * violation of the supplier pattern and leads to runtime exceptions.\n   547→     * This {@link Processor} should be used to keep the {@link StateStore} up-to-date.\n   548→     * The default {@link TimestampExtractor} as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} is used.\n   549→     * <p>\n   550→     * It is not required to connect a global store to the {@link Processor Processors},\n   551→     * or {@link org.apache.kafka.streams.kstream.KTable#transformValues(ValueTransformerWithKeySupplier, String...) * <p>\n * It is a requirement that the processing logic ({@link Topology}) be defined in a deterministic way,\n * as in, the order in which all operators are added must be predictable and the same across all application\n * instances.\n * Topologies are only identical if all operators are added in the same order.\n * If different {@link KafkaStreams} instances of the same application build different topologies the result may be\n * incompatible runtime code and unexpected results or errors\n *\n * @see Topology\n * @see KStream\n * @see KTable\n * @see GlobalKTable\n */\npublic class StreamsBuilder {\n\n    /** The actual topology that is constructed by this StreamsBuilder. */\n    protected final Topology topology;\n\n    /** The topology's internal builder. */\n    protected final InternalTopologyBuilder internalTopologyBuilder;\n\n    protected final InternalStreamsBuilder internalStreamsBuilder;\n\n    public StreamsBuilder() {\n        topology = new Topology();\n        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n        internalStreamsBuilder = new InternalStreamsBuilder(internalTopologyBuilder, false);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@code StreamsBuilder} instance.\n     *\n     * @param topologyConfigs    the streams configs that apply at the topology level. Please refer to {@link TopologyConfig} for more detail\n     */\n    @SuppressWarnings(\"this-escape\")\n    public StreamsBuilder(final TopologyConfig topologyConfigs) {\n        topology = newTopology(topologyConfigs);\n        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n        internalStreamsBuilder = new InternalStreamsBuilder(\n            internalTopologyBuilder,\n            TopologyConfig.InternalConfig.getBoolean(\n                topologyConfigs.originals(),\n                TopologyConfig.InternalConfig.ENABLE_PROCESS_PROCESSVALUE_FIX,\n                false\n            )\n        );\n    }\n\n    protected Topology newTopology(final TopologyConfig topologyConfigs) {\n        return new Topology(topologyConfigs);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic.\n     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, default {@link TimestampExtractor}, and default key and value\n     * deserializers as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * If multiple topics are specified there is no ordering guarantee for records from different topics.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topic the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topic\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final String topic) {\n        return stream(Collections.singleton(topic));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic.\n     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topic the topic names; **StreamsBuilder.build(Properties)** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/StreamsBuilder.java:594): The entry point where users invoke build() with optional properties. It iterates through a priority queue of GraphNodes and calls writeToTopology() on each node to register them with the InternalTopologyBuilder.\\n\\n4. **InternalTopologyBuilder** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/internals/InternalTopologyBuilder.java): The core builder that maintains:\\n   - NodeFactories (ProcessorNodeFactory, SourceNodeFactory, SinkNodeFactory) indexed by node name\\n   - StoreFactory instances for state stores indexed by store name\\n   - State store name to changelog topic mappings\\n   - State store name to source topic mappings\\n\\n5. **InternalTopologyBuilder.buildTopology()** (line 963): Collects all node names (excluding global nodes) and calls the private build(Set<String> nodeGroup) method to construct the complete ProcessorTopology.\\n\\n6. **InternalTopologyBuilder.build(Set<String> nodeGroup)** (line 1012): Creates processor nodes by:\\n   - Iterating through nodeFactories and calling factory.build() to create ProcessorNode instances\\n   - Calling buildProcessorNode() for ProcessorNodeFactory instances to connect state stores\\n   - Constructing source and sink node maps\\n   - Returns a ProcessorTopology instance containing the compiled graph\\n\\n7. **StoreBuilder registration** (line 591-605): StreamsBuilder.addStateStore() wraps the StoreBuilder in StoreBuilderWrapper and delegates to internalStreamsBuilder, which calls InternalTopologyBuilder.addStateStore(). This registers the store factory for later instantiation.\\n\\n8. **InternalTopologyBuilder.buildProcessorNode()** (line 1118): For each processor node, this method:\\n   - Connects node predecessors and children to build the processor graph\\n   - For each state store name, retrieves the StoreFactory\\n   - Calls storeFactory.builder().build() to instantiate the actual StateStore\\n   - Tracks changelog topics if logging is enabled\\n   - Stores the built StateStore in stateStoreMap\\n\\n9. **ProcessorTopology constructor** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/internals/ProcessorTopology.java:49-77): Receives the compiled processor nodes, source/sink node maps, state stores, and global state stores. Sets the thread ID from current thread context\\n    - Initializes the InternalProcessorContext\\n    - Calls init() on the underlying Processor or FixedKeyProcessor instance\\n    - Marks the node as open for processing\\n\\nKey state store building classes:\\n- **StoreBuilder** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/state/StoreBuilder.java): Interface for building StateStore instances with optional caching and logging\\n- **StoreFactory** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/internals/StoreFactory.java): Internal wrapper around StoreBuilder that allows post-topology configuration before stores are instantiated\\n- **ProcessorNodeFactory classes**: Abstract NodeFactory subclasses (ProcessorNodeFactory, SourceNodeFactory, SinkNodeFactory) that build corresponding ProcessorNode instances from factories\\n\\nThe entire flow enables delayed state store instantiation (stores are created during buildProcessorNode, not when topology is added) while maintaining deterministic topology ordering through topologically-sorted nodeFactories.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":212,"cache_read_input_tokens":61846,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":212},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ea7e913b-bb43-4b99-aa7b-34e9a0dca399","uuid":"52b97894-d4da-419f-a738-a379f8ca37c1"}
